## GHSA-4j6x-2764-m8gh ¬∑ github.com/rancher/rancher

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Go ¬∑ **HIGH** 8.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `PRIVILEGE_ESCALATION‚ÜíROLE`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an over-inclusive team membership expansion logic in the GitHub App authentication provider. When listing teams for a user, the system iterated through all teams within an organization that the user was a member of, rather than only the specific teams the user was actually a member of. This meant that if a user was a member of an organization, they would implicitly gain access to all teams within that organization, even if they were not explicitly assigned to them.

### Impact

An attacker could gain unauthorized access to resources and projects associated with GitHub teams they were not explicitly a member of, simply by being a member of the parent GitHub organization. This could lead to privilege escalation and unauthorized data access.

### Key diff

```
--- a/pkg/auth/providers/githubapp/github_data.go
+++ b/pkg/auth/providers/githubapp/github_data.go
@@ -119,9 +119,13 @@ func (g *gitHubAppData) listOrgs() []common.GitHubAccount {
 func (g *gitHubAppData) listTeamsForUser(username string) []common.GitHubAccount {
 	var accounts []common.GitHubAccount
 
-	for orgName := range g.members[username].orgs {
+	for orgName, teamNames := range g.members[username].orgs {
 		org := g.orgs[orgName]
-		for teamName, team := range org.teams {
+		for _, teamName := range teamNames {
+			team, ok := org.teams[teamName]
+			if !ok {
+				continue
+			}
 			accounts = append(accounts, common.GitHubAccount{Name: teamName, Login: team.login, AvatarURL: org.avatarURL, ID: team.id, HTMLURL: team.htmlURL})
 		}
 	}
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the `listTeamsForUser` function to correctly filter teams. Instead of iterating through all teams in an organization, it now iterates only through the teams explicitly associated with the user within that organization. Additionally, a mechanism was added to trigger a one-time refresh of all user group principals for GitHub App users upon startup, ensuring existing incorrect memberships are updated.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 27 occurrences**
> Languages: Java, Python, JavaScript, Go, Ruby, PHP

## GHSA-5qfp-32cf-69jh ¬∑ surrealdb

2026-07-01 ¬∑ RUST ¬∑ **HIGH** 8.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `MISSING_AUTH‚ÜíENDPOINT`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from two issues: the HTTP /rpc `sessions` method allowed enumeration of attached session UUIDs, and there was insufficient authorization enforcement for client-supplied session IDs. An attacker could observe or guess a victim's session UUID and then use it to impersonate them, even after the victim had authenticated.

### Impact

An anonymous attacker could enumerate active session UUIDs and then hijack authenticated user sessions, gaining full access to the victim's account and data.

### Key diff

```
--- surrealdb/server/src/rpc/http.rs
+++ surrealdb/server/src/rpc/http.rs
@@ -67,6 +78,78 @@ impl Http {
 		}
 	}
+
+	/// Verify that the caller of an HTTP `/rpc` request is authorised to use
+	/// a client-supplied session id.
+	fn verify_caller_for_session(
+		&self,
+		session_id: Uuid,
+		caller_auth: &Option<Auth>,
+	) -> DbResult<()>
+	{
+		// Ephemeral ids (from any concurrent request) are not user-targetable and return
+		// `session_not_found` to avoid confirming their existence.
+		if self.ephemeral_sessions.contains_key(&session_id) {
+			return Err(session_not_found());
+		}
+
+		let session = match self.sessions.get(&session_id) {
+			Some(session) => session,
+			None => return Err(session_not_found()),
+		};
+
+		let session_auth = session.read().await.au.clone();
+
+		// If the stored session has not yet been authenticated (`Session.au` at `Level::No`), any
+		// caller may reach into it. This preserves the standard `attach` followed by
+		// `signin`/`authenticate` flow: `attach` creates an anonymous session and a subsequent
+		// authentication call promotes it to the caller's principal. An unauthenticated session
+		// carries no elevated privileges, so this is safe given that session UUIDs are 128-bit
+		// random and cannot be enumerated ‚Äî see the [`RpcProtocol::sessions`] override.
+		if session_auth.level == Level::None {
+			return Ok(());
+		}
+
+		// Once the stored session is bound to a principal, the caller's request-level principal
+		// fingerprint (`actor id` + `Level`) must exactly match the session's current `Session.au`
+		// principal. Roles are intentionally excluded from the comparison so that legitimate re-auth
+		// with a different role set for the same identity still matches.
+		let caller_principal = match caller_auth {
+			Some(auth) => auth.principal(),
+			None => return Err(session_not_found()),
+		};
+
+		let session_principal = session_auth.principal();
+
+		if caller_principal.id != session_principal.id
+			|| caller_principal.level != session_principal.level
+		{
+			return Err(session_not_found());
+		}
+
+		Ok(())
+	}
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces two main security measures: it explicitly rejects the `sessions` RPC method to prevent enumeration of session UUIDs, and it implements a strict authorization check (`Http::verify_caller_for_session`). This check ensures that once a session is authenticated, subsequent requests targeting that session UUID must present matching authentication credentials (actor ID and level) to prevent unauthorized access.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 35 occurrences**

## GHSA-4vgr-h27g-cf9p ¬∑ surrealdb

2026-07-01 ¬∑ RUST ¬∑ **HIGH** 8.1 ¬∑ Pattern: `RACE_CONDITION‚ÜíTOCTOU`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from the `RpcProtocol`'s `session_map` using `Option<Uuid>` as a key, allowing `None` to be a valid session ID. This design, combined with how HTTP RPC requests were handled, meant that a client could potentially create a session with `None` as its ID. Subsequently, if another client's request was processed without an explicit session ID, it would implicitly use the `None` session, leading to a race condition where an unauthenticated client could gain control over a privileged session.

### Impact

An attacker could exploit this race condition to escalate privileges, potentially gaining unauthorized access to sensitive data or performing actions as a more privileged user.

### Key diff

```
--- a/surrealdb/core/src/rpc/protocol.rs
+++ b/surrealdb/core/src/rpc/protocol.rs
@@ -57,17 +57,14 @@ pub trait RpcProtocol {
 
 	/// A pointer to all active sessions
-	fn session_map(&self) -> &HashMap<Option<Uuid>, Arc<RwLock<Session>>>;
+	fn session_map(&self) -> &HashMap<Uuid, Arc<RwLock<Session>>>;
 
 	/// Registers a new session with the given ID
-	async fn attach(&self, session_id: Option<Uuid>) -> Result<DbResult, surrealdb_types::Error> {
-		let mut session = Session::default().with_rt(Self::LQ_SUPPORT);
-		session.id = session_id;
-		match session_id {
-			Some(id) => {
-				if self.session_map().contains_key(&Some(id)) {
-					return Err(session_exists(id));
-				}
-				self.session_map().insert(Some(id), Arc::new(RwLock::new(session)));
-				Ok(DbResult::Other(PublicValue::None))
-			}
-			None => Err(invalid_params("Expected a session ID")),
-		}
+	async fn attach(&self, session_id: Uuid) -> Result<DbResult, surrealdb_types::Error> {
+		if self.session_map().contains_key(&session_id) {
+			return Err(session_exists(session_id));
+		}
+		let mut session = Session::default().with_rt(Self::LQ_SUPPORT);
+		session.id = Some(session_id);
+		self.session_map().insert(session_id, Arc::new(RwLock::new(session)));
+		Ok(DbResult::Other(PublicValue::None))
 	}
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the `session_map` to only accept `Uuid` (non-optional) as keys, preventing `None` from being a valid session ID. It also ensures that `attach` and `detach` methods explicitly require a `Uuid` and handles cases where a client provides `None` for these methods by returning an error, thus eliminating the possibility of a `None` session ID being created or used implicitly.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 7 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript, Go, Python, RUST
> ‚Üí GHSA-gj9q-8w99-mp8j
> ‚Üí GHSA-rmx9-2pp3-xhcr
> ‚Üí GHSA-5h3g-6xhh-rg6p
> ‚Üí GHSA-h3ww-q6xx-w7x3
> ‚Üí GHSA-r95r-rj6r-c39x
> ‚Üí GHSA-7fq5-7wr8-rjwj

üîó [View commit](https://github.com/surrealdb/surrealdb/commit/2f53e6e86d1b87e38300e714cfd7aede1abe4c3d)

## GHSA-5rff-8f7c-8jmw ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the 'nAtoms' variable, parsed from user-controlled input in ORCA files, was not properly validated. A malicious or malformed file could specify a large or negative 'nAtoms' value, leading to an undersized buffer allocation or an integer overflow, which was then used to write coordinate data.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious ORCA file that, when processed by Open Babel, would cause an out-of-bounds write. This could lead to a denial of service (application crash), information disclosure, or potentially arbitrary code execution.

### Key diff

```
-                    nAtoms = atoi((char*)vs[4].c_str());
+                    if (vs.size() > 4)
+                        nAtoms = atoi((char*)vs[4].c_str());
+                    if (nAtoms < 0 || nAtoms > 10000000)
+                        nAtoms = 0;
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds validation for the 'nAtoms' value, clamping it to a sane range (0 to 10,000,000) to prevent excessively large or negative values. It also ensures that the 'confCoords' buffer is allocated only if 'nAtoms' is positive and that writes to this buffer are bounded by 'nAtoms'. Additionally, it ensures 'confCoords' is properly initialized and freed.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 28 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Ruby, Python, C#, JavaScript, RUST, Java

## GHSA-7h6r-6p76-68c9 ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The application did not properly validate the number of translation vectors read from input files (MOPAC, MSI, Gaussian formats). It would increment `numTranslationVectors` and use it as an index into the `translationVectors` array without checking if the index exceeded the array's allocated size, which is fixed at 3.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious input file that, when parsed, would cause an out-of-bounds write to memory. This could lead to a denial of service (application crash) or potentially arbitrary code execution if the overwritten memory region is critical.

### Key diff

```
-                translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
+                if (numTranslationVectors < 3)
+                  translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds a check before assigning to `translationVectors`. It ensures that `numTranslationVectors` is less than 3 (the maximum allowed size) before incrementing it and using it as an index. This prevents writing beyond the allocated buffer.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 28 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Ruby, Python, C#, JavaScript, RUST, Java

## GHSA-8qxc-57hf-hc9j ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíSTACK`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the `strcat` function was used to concatenate strings into fixed-size buffers (`full_coord_path` and `coord_file`) without checking if the destination buffer had sufficient space. If the combined length of the strings exceeded the buffer's capacity, it would lead to a buffer overflow.

### Impact

An attacker providing a specially crafted PQS file could cause a buffer overflow, potentially leading to a denial of service (application crash) or arbitrary code execution, depending on the memory layout and overwritten data.

### Key diff

```
-                strcat(full_coord_path,coord_file);
-                full_coord_path[sizeof(full_coord_path) - 1] = '\0';
+                strncat(full_coord_path, coord_file,
+                        sizeof(full_coord_path) - strlen(full_coord_path) - 1);
```

### Fix summary

The patch replaces the unsafe `strcat` calls with `strncat`. This function limits the number of characters appended to the destination buffer, preventing an overflow by ensuring that the buffer's capacity is not exceeded when concatenating strings.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 5 occurrences**
> Languages: Python, C#
> ‚Üí GHSA-2689-5p89-6j3j
> ‚Üí GHSA-f4qm-vj5j-9xpw
> ‚Üí GHSA-vjg6-gm8m-v5g6
> ‚Üí GHSA-f29h-2h58-48r7

üîó [View commit](https://github.com/openbabel/openbabel/commit/2a7d2cda8bd47daade2e555e34b69651a2e132ef)

## GHSA-f29h-2h58-48r7 ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíSTACK`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the `strcat` function was used to concatenate strings into fixed-size buffers (`full_coord_path` and `coord_file`) without checking the buffer's remaining capacity. If the combined length of the strings exceeded the buffer size, it would lead to an out-of-bounds write.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted PQS file that, when parsed, would cause the application to write data beyond the allocated buffer, potentially leading to a denial of service (crash) or arbitrary code execution.

### Key diff

```
-                strcat(full_coord_path,coord_file);
-                full_coord_path[sizeof(full_coord_path) - 1] = '\0';
+                strncat(full_coord_path, coord_file,
+                        sizeof(full_coord_path) - strlen(full_coord_path) - 1);
```

### Fix summary

The patch replaces the unsafe `strcat` calls with `strncat`. `strncat` is used with a calculated maximum length to ensure that the concatenation does not exceed the buffer's bounds, preventing out-of-bounds writes.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 5 occurrences**

## GHSA-f8h2-c479-vqxf ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The application failed to validate the number of translation vectors being read from input files (MOPAC, MSI, Gaussian formats) before writing them to a fixed-size array. This allowed an attacker to supply more translation vectors than the array could hold, leading to an out-of-bounds write.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially achieve denial of service (application crash) or arbitrary code execution by corrupting memory outside the intended buffer.

### Key diff

```
- translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
+ if (numTranslationVectors < 3)
+   translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds bounds checks before writing to the `translationVectors` array. It ensures that `numTranslationVectors` does not exceed 3 (the presumed maximum capacity) before incrementing it and setting new vector values, preventing writes beyond the array's allocated memory.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 28 occurrences**

## GHSA-jg3h-pv7c-4f9c ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The code was attempting to write translation vectors into a fixed-size array (translationVectors) without performing bounds checking. If an input file (MOPAC, MSI, Gaussian) contained more than 3 translation vectors, the program would write past the end of the allocated array.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted input file to cause an out-of-bounds write, potentially leading to a denial of service (crash) or arbitrary code execution by corrupting adjacent memory.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/formats/mopacformat.cpp
+++ b/src/formats/mopacformat.cpp
@@ -167,7 +167,8 @@ namespace OpenBabel
                 y = atof((char*)vs[3].c_str());
                 z = atof((char*)vs[4].c_str());
 
-                translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
+                if (numTranslationVectors < 3)
+                  translationVectors[numTranslationVectors++].Set(x, y, z);
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds explicit bounds checks (numTranslationVectors < 3) before writing to the translationVectors array in multiple locations across mopacformat.cpp, msiformat.cpp, and gaussformat.cpp. This ensures that no more than 3 translation vectors are ever stored, preventing the out-of-bounds write.

## GHSA-jr2x-6qf6-q5mc ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `NULL_DEREF‚ÜíCRASH`

### Root cause

The vulnerabilities stemmed from pointers being declared but not always initialized to a safe value (like nullptr) or checked before dereference. In MSI format parsing, `atom` could be dereferenced before being assigned. In PQS format, `pFormat` could be uninitialized if no matching format string was found. In GRO format, `res` could be null if an atom lacked residue information.

### Impact

An attacker providing specially crafted input files (MSI, PQS, or GRO) could cause the application to crash due to a null pointer dereference, leading to a denial of service. In some cases, it might lead to information disclosure or arbitrary code execution, though a crash is the most direct impact.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/formats/msiformat.cpp
+++ b/src/formats/msiformat.cpp
@@ -107,7 +107,7 @@ namespace OpenBabel
     unsigned int startBondAtom, endBondAtom, bondOrder;
     bool atomRecord = false;
     bool bondRecord = false;
-    OBAtom *atom;
+    OBAtom *atom = nullptr;
 //    OBBond *bond;
     vector<string> vs;
     const SpaceGroup *sg;
@@ -190,6 +191,11 @@ namespace OpenBabel
             tokenize(vs, buffer);
             // size should be 6 -- need a test here
             if (vs.size() != 6) return false; // timvdm 18/06/2008
+            // CVE-2022-44451: an atom record may contain XYZ before
+            // the ACL line that normally creates `atom`. Skip the
+            // coordinates rather than dereferencing an unset pointer.
+            if (atom == nullptr)
+              continue;
             vs[3].erase(0,1); // remove ( character
             vs[5].erase(vs[5].length()-2, 2); // remove trailing )) characters
             atom->SetVector(atof(vs[3].c_str()),
```

### Fix summary

The patches initialize pointers (`atom`, `pFormat`, `res`) to `nullptr` upon declaration. They also add explicit checks for `nullptr` before dereferencing these pointers, ensuring that operations are only performed on valid objects and providing fallback behavior or error handling when a pointer is null.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 16 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript, RUST, Go, Python
> ‚Üí GHSA-f37v-82c4-4x64
> ‚Üí GHSA-48m6-486p-9j8p
> ‚Üí GHSA-fpjq-c37h-cqcv
> ‚Üí GHSA-p9mg-74mg-cwwr
> ‚Üí GHSA-j59f-x285-69jx

### Impact


### Fix summary

## GHSA-mw5r-wq2m-397c ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `NULL_DEREF‚ÜíCRASH`

### Root cause

The vulnerabilities stemmed from pointers being used without proper initialization or checks for null values. In `msiformat.cpp`, an `OBAtom` pointer could be dereferenced before being assigned. In `PQSformat.cpp`, an `OBFormat` pointer was not initialized, leading to potential dereference of garbage memory. In `groformat.cpp`, an `OBResidue` pointer could be null if an atom lacked residue information, but was still dereferenced.

### Impact

An attacker could cause a denial of service (application crash) due to dereferencing uninitialized or null pointers. In some cases, this could potentially lead to arbitrary code execution, though a crash is the most direct impact.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/formats/msiformat.cpp
+++ b/src/formats/msiformat.cpp
@@ -107,7 +107,7 @@ namespace OpenBabel
     unsigned int startBondAtom, endBondAtom, bondOrder;
     bool atomRecord = false;
     bool bondRecord = false;
-    OBAtom *atom;
+    OBAtom *atom = nullptr;
 //    OBBond *bond;
     vector<string> vs;
     const SpaceGroup *sg;
@@ -190,6 +191,11 @@ namespace OpenBabel
             tokenize(vs, buffer);
             // size should be 6 -- need a test here
             if (vs.size() != 6) return false; // timvdm 18/06/2008
+            // CVE-2022-44451: an atom record may contain XYZ before
+            // the ACL line that normally creates `atom`. Skip the
+            // coordinates rather than dereferencing an unset pointer.
+            if (atom == nullptr)
+              continue;
             vs[3].erase(0,1); // remove ( character
             vs[5].erase(vs[5].length()-2, 2); // remove trailing )) characters
             atom->SetVector(atof(vs[3].c_str()),
```

### Fix summary

The patches initialize pointers to `nullptr` at declaration and add explicit null checks before dereferencing them. For `msiformat.cpp`, a check ensures `atom` is not null before setting its vector. For `PQSformat.cpp`, `pFormat` is initialized to `nullptr` and checked before use, returning `false` if no valid format is found. For `groformat.cpp`, `res` is initialized to `nullptr` and its dereferences are guarded by null checks, providing default values if `res` is null.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 16 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript, RUST, Go, Python

## GHSA-rj4c-r689-cm87 ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the 'orcaformat.cpp' parser did not properly validate the 'Number of atoms' value read from ORCA input files. An attacker could provide a large or negative value for 'nAtoms', leading to an undersized or oversized buffer allocation for 'confCoords', and subsequent out-of-bounds writes when populating the conformer coordinates.

### Impact

An attacker could achieve denial of service (application crash) or potentially arbitrary code execution by corrupting heap memory due to the out-of-bounds write.

### Key diff

```
-                    nAtoms = atoi((char*)vs[4].c_str());
+                    if (vs.size() > 4)
+                        nAtoms = atoi((char*)vs[4].c_str());
+                    if (nAtoms < 0 || nAtoms > 10000000)
+                        nAtoms = 0;
```

### Fix summary

The patch adds validation for the 'nAtoms' value, clamping it to a sane range (0 to 10,000,000) to prevent malicious values from driving out-of-bounds allocations and writes. It also adds checks to ensure 'confCoords' is not null and the index 'i' is within 'nAtoms' before writing, and handles the cleanup of 'confCoords' more robustly.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 28 occurrences**
> Languages: Go, Ruby, Python, C#, JavaScript, RUST, Java

## GHSA-vjg6-gm8m-v5g6 ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíSTACK`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the sscanf function was used to parse user-controlled input into fixed-size buffers (attr and val) without specifying a maximum width. If the input string for either the attribute or value was longer than 31 characters, sscanf would write past the end of the allocated buffer.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted MOL2 file that, when parsed, would lead to an out-of-bounds write. This could result in a denial of service (application crash) or potentially arbitrary code execution, depending on the overwritten memory region.

### Key diff

```
-            sscanf(buffer, "########## %[^:]:%s", attr, val);
+            sscanf(buffer, "########## %31[^:]:%31s", attr, val);
```

### Fix summary

The patch addresses the vulnerability by adding width specifiers (%31[^:] and %31s) to the sscanf format string. This limits the number of characters read into the 'attr' and 'val' buffers to 31, preventing an out-of-bounds write.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 5 occurrences**
> Languages: Python, C#
> ‚Üí GHSA-2689-5p89-6j3j
> ‚Üí GHSA-f4qm-vj5j-9xpw
> ‚Üí GHSA-8qxc-57hf-hc9j
> ‚Üí GHSA-f29h-2h58-48r7

üîó [View commit](https://github.com/openbabel/openbabel/commit/4110d59ada242139fb02098e1e1faff57ac4dd51)

## GHSA-vr3p-gg26-45v9 ¬∑ openbabel

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Python ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.8 ¬∑ Pattern: `BUFFER_OVERFLOW‚ÜíHEAP`

### Root cause

The vulnerability in `gaussformat.cpp` was due to using a fixed-size `char` array for `coords_type` and then using `strncpy` and `strcat` without proper bounds checking. If the input string was longer than 24 characters, `strcat` would write past the buffer's end. In `CSRformat.cpp`, `strncpy` was used without ensuring the source string length did not exceed the destination buffer's capacity minus one for the null terminator, leading to potential out-of-bounds writes if `strlen(input)` was greater than `size - 1`.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted input file that, when parsed, would cause an out-of-bounds write. This could lead to denial of service (application crash), information disclosure, or potentially arbitrary code execution, depending on the overwritten memory region.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/formats/gaussformat.cpp
+++ b/src/formats/gaussformat.cpp
-    char coords_type[25];
+    std::string coords_type;
-            strncpy (coords_type, vs[0].c_str(), 24);
-            strcat (coords_type, " orientation:");
+            coords_type = vs[0] + " orientation:";

--- a/src/formats/CSRformat.cpp
+++ b/src/formats/CSRformat.cpp
-    strncpy(output, input, strlen(input));
+    size_t len = strlen(input);
+    if (len > static_cast<size_t>(size - 1))
+      len = static_cast<size_t>(size - 1);
+    memcpy(output, input, len);
```

### Fix summary

The patch addresses the `gaussformat.cpp` issue by replacing the fixed-size `char` array with `std::string` for `coords_type`, eliminating the need for manual buffer management with `strncpy` and `strcat`. In `CSRformat.cpp`, `strncpy` was replaced with `memcpy` and an explicit length check was added to ensure that no more than `size - 1` bytes are copied from the input string, preventing an out-of-bounds write.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 28 occurrences**

## GHSA-jxpm-75mh-9fp7 ¬∑ oras.land/oras-go/v2

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Go ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.5 ¬∑ Pattern: `SSRF‚ÜíINTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The oras-go library did not validate the 'Location' header returned by a registry during a blob upload. An attacker-controlled registry could redirect the client to an arbitrary external host, causing the client to forward its credentials (e.g., authentication tokens) to the attacker's server.

### Impact

An attacker could steal authentication credentials or other sensitive information by redirecting the client to a malicious server, potentially leading to unauthorized access to other services or data.

### Key diff

```
--- a/registry/remote/repository.go
+++ b/registry/remote/repository.go
@@ -894,6 +914,15 @@ func (s *blobStore) completePushAfterInitialPost(ctx context.Context, req *http.
 		if reqPort == "443" && locationHostname == reqHostname && locationPort == "" {
 			location.Host = locationHostname + ":" + reqPort
 		}
+		// Validate the Location stays on the same host to prevent credentials from
+		// being forwarded to an attacker-controlled endpoint.
+		// Reference: https://github.com/oras-project/oras-go/security/advisories/GHSA-jxpm-75mh-9fp7
+		if !sameUploadHost(location, req.URL) {
+			return fmt.Errorf("blob upload Location %q is on a different host than the registry %q", location.Host, req.URL.Host)
+		}
+		if req.URL.Scheme == "https" && location.Scheme != "https" {
+			return fmt.Errorf("blob upload Location %q downgrades scheme from https", location.Host)
+		}
 		url := location.String()
 		req, err = http.NewRequestWithContext(ctx, http.MethodPut, url, content)
 		if err != nil
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new function `sameUploadHost` to validate that the 'Location' header's host matches the original request's host, including canonicalizing ports. It also checks that the scheme does not downgrade from HTTPS. If these checks fail, an error is returned, preventing credential forwarding.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 61 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript, Go, Python, PHP, RUST, Erlang

## GHSA-q729-696q-g9pq ¬∑ surrealdb

2026-07-01 ¬∑ RUST ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.5 ¬∑ Pattern: `DOS‚ÜíRESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed in the JSON parser's handling of deeply nested objects and arrays. Without proper recursion limits, a maliciously crafted input with excessive nesting could cause the parser to consume an unbounded amount of memory or CPU, leading to a crash.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted JSON input to the SurrealDB server, causing the server process to crash or become unresponsive, leading to a denial of service for legitimate users.

### Key diff

```
--- a/surrealdb/core/src/syn/parser/value.rs
+++ b/surrealdb/core/src/syn/parser/value.rs
@@ -9,7 +9,7 @@ use crate::syn::error::bail;
 use crate::syn::lexer::Lexer;
 use crate::syn::lexer::compound::{self, Numeric};
 use crate::syn::parser::mac::{expected, expected_whitespace};
-use crate::syn::parser::unexpected;
+use crate::syn::parser::{enter_object_recursion, unexpected};
 use crate::syn::token::{Span, TokenKind, t};
 use crate::types::{
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a recursion depth limit for parsing objects and arrays. It wraps the parsing logic for these structures within an `enter_object_recursion!` macro, which likely increments a counter and checks against a predefined maximum depth, preventing infinite or excessively deep recursion.

## GHSA-wjjj-24cx-f28g ¬∑ surrealdb

2026-07-01 ¬∑ RUST ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.5 ¬∑ Pattern: `DOS‚ÜíRESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The vulnerability existed because the server would panic and abort the entire process if a `use` RPC call attempted to set a database without a namespace being previously established in the session. This unhandled panic, combined with the `panic = 'abort'` setting, led to a server-wide crash.

### Impact

An unauthenticated remote attacker could send a specially crafted RPC `use` call to the SurrealDB server, causing the entire server process to crash and resulting in a denial of service for all legitimate users.

### Key diff

```
- let ns = session.ns.clone().expect("namespace should be set");
+ let Some(ns) = session.ns.clone() else {
+    return Err(invalid_params(
+        "Cannot set database without first selecting a namespace".to_string(),
+    ));
+ };
```

### Fix summary

The patch addresses the vulnerability by replacing the `.expect()` call with a `let Some(ns) = ... else { return Err(...) };` construct. This change ensures that if a `use` call attempts to set a database without a namespace, the server returns a clean error message instead of panicking and aborting the process.

## GHSA-32h4-44jj-c5vx ¬∑ org.keycloak:keycloak-services

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Java ¬∑ **HIGH** 7.3 ¬∑ Pattern: `PRIVILEGE_ESCALATION‚ÜíROLE`

### Root cause

The Keycloak admin API endpoints for managing client and realm scope mappings did not properly enforce authorization checks. Specifically, when adding or deleting scope mappings, the system failed to verify if the authenticated user had the necessary permissions to map the specified roles, allowing unauthorized users to manipulate scope mappings.

### Impact

An attacker with administrative access but insufficient privileges could escalate their privileges by mapping roles they shouldn't have access to, potentially gaining control over clients or realms they are not authorized to manage.

### Key diff

```
--- a/services/src/main/java/org/keycloak/services/resources/admin/ScopeMappedClientResource.java
+++ b/services/src/main/java/org/keycloak/services/resources/admin/ScopeMappedClientResource.java
@@ -167,6 +167,7 @@ public void addClientScopeMapping(List<RoleRepresentation> roles) {
             if (roleModel == null) {
                 throw new NotFoundException("Role not found");
             }
+            auth.roles().requireMapClientScope(roleModel);
             scopeContainer.addScopeMapping(roleModel);
         }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces explicit authorization checks using `auth.roles().requireMapClientScope(roleModel)` before adding or deleting scope mappings. It also filters roles during deletion using `auth.roles()::canMapClientScope` to ensure only authorized roles are processed, thereby enforcing proper privilege separation.

> ‚ö° **Pattern match ‚Äî 27 occurrences**
> Languages: Java, Python, JavaScript, Go, Ruby, PHP

## GHSA-vh4v-2xq2-g5cg ¬∑ oras.land/oras-go/v2

2026-07-01 ¬∑ Go ¬∑ **MODERATE** 0.0 ¬∑ Pattern: `CREDENTIAL_LEAK‚ÜíLOG_EXPOSURE`

### Root cause

The ORAS Go client would forward Authorization headers (containing registry credentials) to redirected URLs even if the redirect crossed an HTTP origin (scheme, host, or port). The standard library's default behavior only strips sensitive headers when the hostname changes, leaving other origin changes vulnerable.

### Impact

An attacker could redirect a client to a malicious server on a different port or scheme, causing the client to unintentionally send its registry credentials to the attacker. This could lead to unauthorized access to private container images or other sensitive resources.

### Key diff

```
--- a/registry/remote/auth/client.go
+++ b/registry/remote/auth/client.go
@@ -137,7 +137,50 @@ func (c *Client) send(req *http.Request) (*http.Response, error) {
 	for key, values := range c.Header {
 		req.Header[key] = append(req.Header[key], values...)
 	}
-	return c.client().Do(req)
+	client := c.client()
+	clientCopy := *client
+	checkRedirect := client.CheckRedirect
+	clientCopy.CheckRedirect = func(req *http.Request, via []*http.Request) error {
+		if len(via) > 0 && !sameHTTPOrigin(via[len(via)-1].URL, req.URL) {
+			req.Header.Del("Authorization")
+		}
+		if checkRedirect != nil {
+			return checkRedirect(req, via)
+		}
+		return nil
+	}
+	return clientCopy.Do(req)
 }
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the HTTP client's `CheckRedirect` function to explicitly remove the 'Authorization' header if a redirect crosses an HTTP origin (scheme, host, or port). Additionally, it prevents sending credentials to a different origin if the authentication challenge itself comes from a redirected, different origin.
